## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most naturally maps to constitutive stress–strain relations with thermal dependence (thermoelasticity, plasticity with thermal softening, and empirical flow-stress models used in materials processing). Temperature typically enters through a temperature-dependent modulus, yield stress, or softening factor multiplying the strain response.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with E(T))
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial with thermal coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate nonlinearity with thermal dependence)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changing exponentially with temperature)
- Thermal strain offset (thermoelastic with expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type (implicit/compliance form solved for sigma): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (captures elastic + nonlinear/plastic strain; temperature can enter via c0(T), c1(T))
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 + epsilon)**c3 (strain hardening with thermal weakening/strengthening)
- Ludwik/Hollomon with thermal factor: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T) * epsilon**c3 (yield/offset plus temperature-scaled hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature-dependent saturation: sigma = c0 + (c1 + c2 * T) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening; saturation level varies with T)
- Bilinear elastic–plastic (piecewise via Max): sigma = c0 * epsilon - c1 * Max(epsilon - c2, 0) (elastic slope then reduced tangent modulus after yield strain c2)
- Elastic-perfectly plastic with thermal yield: sigma = Min((c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, c2 + c3 * T) (linear elastic capped by temperature-dependent yield stress)
- Johnson–Cook-like (reduced, no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4))**c5 (empirical flow stress with thermal softening)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-type small variant) with thermal shear modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) (captures geometric/material nonlinearity with T-dependent stiffness)
- Rational softening/hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + c2 * epsilon) (initially linear, then saturates/softens at larger strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature dependence usually appears as a prefactor E(T) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal softening of stiffness or strength → multiplicative factors like exp(c*T) or (1 - c*(T-c0))**n reducing sigma as T increases.
- Thermal expansion effects → stress depends on mechanical strain (epsilon minus a T-dependent offset), i.e., sigma ∝ (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)).
- Yielding/plastic onset → piecewise or Min/Max structures that cap sigma at a yield level or change slope after a yield strain.
- Strain hardening → sigma increasing concavely/convexly with epsilon via epsilon**n or (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) (Voce-type saturation).
- Saturation of flow stress at large strain → asymptotic forms like 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) or rational epsilon/(1+c*epsilon).
- Coupled thermomechanical response → allow both additive (sigma = f(epsilon)+g(T)) and multiplicative (sigma = f(epsilon)*g(T)) decompositions; multiplicative is common for softening factors.
- Temperature-dependent yield stress → yield level modeled as (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T), producing lower/higher plateaus across T.
- Nonlinear elasticity before yield → include epsilon**2, epsilon**3 terms with coefficients that vary with T to reflect anharmonic lattice effects.

The key basis functions in GT are:
